</td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="noprint" style="text-align:center"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Soccerball_current_event.svg/33px-Soccerball_current_event.svg.png" decoding="async" width="33" height="33" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Soccerball_current_event.svg/50px-Soccerball_current_event.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Soccerball_current_event.svg/66px-Soccerball_current_event.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="60" data-file-height="60" /> <i><a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_Cardiff_City_F.C._season" title="2019–20 Cardiff City F.C. season">Current season</a></i></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Cardiff City Football Club</b> (<a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh</a>: <i lang="cy">Clwb Pêl-droed Dinas Caerdydd</i>) is a professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a> club based in <a href="/wiki/Cardiff" title="Cardiff">Cardiff</a>, Wales. It competes in the <a href="/wiki/EFL_Championship" title="EFL Championship">Championship</a>, the second tier of the <a href="/wiki/English_football_league_system" title="English football league system">English football league system</a>. Founded in 1899 as Riverside A.F.C., the club changed its name to Cardiff City in 1908 and entered the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Football_League" title="Southern Football League">Southern Football League</a> in 1910 before joining the <a href="/wiki/English_Football_League" title="English Football League">English Football League</a> in 1920. The team have spent 17 seasons in the top tier of English football since, the longest period being between 1921 and 1929. Their most recent season in the top flight was the <a href="/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_Premier_League" title="2018–19 Premier League">2018–19 Premier League season</a>.
</p><p>Cardiff is the only team from outside England to have won the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a>, doing so in <a href="/wiki/1927_FA_Cup_Final" title="1927 FA Cup Final">1927</a>. They have also reached three other cup finals in English competitions, the <a href="/wiki/1925_FA_Cup_Final" title="1925 FA Cup Final">1925 FA Cup Final</a> against <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_United_F.C." title="Sheffield United F.C.">Sheffield United</a>, the <a href="/wiki/2008_FA_Cup_Final" title="2008 FA Cup Final">2008 FA Cup Final</a> against <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_F.C." title="Portsmouth F.C.">Portsmouth</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2012_Football_League_Cup_Final" title="2012 Football League Cup Final">2012 Football League Cup Final</a> against <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a>, suffering defeat on each occasion. They have won the <a href="/wiki/Welsh_Cup" title="Welsh Cup">Welsh Cup</a> on 22 occasions, making them the second most successful team in the competition's history behind <a href="/wiki/Wrexham_A.F.C." title="Wrexham A.F.C.">Wrexham</a>.
</p><p>With the exception of a short period this century, the team have played in home colours of blue and white since 1908, which gives them the nickname "The Bluebirds". Cardiff's first permanent ground was <a href="/wiki/Ninian_Park" title="Ninian Park">Ninian Park</a> opened in 1910; it remained in use for 99 years until the club moved into the <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_Stadium" title="Cardiff City Stadium">Cardiff City Stadium</a> in 2009. Cardiff have long-standing rivalries with nearby clubs <a href="/wiki/Swansea_City_A.F.C." title="Swansea City A.F.C.">Swansea City</a>, known as the <a href="/wiki/South_Wales_derby" title="South Wales derby">South Wales derby</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bristol_City_F.C." title="Bristol City F.C.">Bristol City</a>, known as the <a href="/wiki/Severnside_derby" title="Severnside derby">Severnside derby</a>. The club's record appearance holder is <a href="/wiki/Billy_Hardy_(footballer)" title="Billy Hardy (footballer)">Billy Hardy</a>, who made 590 appearances in a 20-year playing spell with Cardiff, and their record goalscorer is <a href="/wiki/Len_Davies" title="Len Davies">Len Davies</a> with 179 goals.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cardiff_City_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Cardiff_City_F.C." title="History of Cardiff City F.C.">History of Cardiff City F.C.</a></div>
<h3><span id="Early_years_.281899.E2.80.931920.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years_(1899–1920)">Early years (1899–1920)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cardiff_City_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early years (1899–1920)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following a meeting at the home of <a href="/wiki/Lithography" title="Lithography">lithographic</a> artist <a href="/wiki/Bartley_Wilson" class="mw-redirect" title="Bartley Wilson">Bartley Wilson</a> in Cardiff,<sup id="cite_ref-Hayes208_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hayes208-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> the club was founded in 1899 as Riverside A.F.C. as a way of keeping players from the Riverside Cricket Club together and in shape during the winter months.<sup id="cite_ref-obscure_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-obscure-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hayes5_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hayes5-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> In their first season, they played <a href="/wiki/Exhibition_game" title="Exhibition game">friendlies</a> against local sides at their <a href="/wiki/Sophia_Gardens" title="Sophia Gardens">Sophia Gardens</a> ground. In 1900 they joined the Cardiff &amp; District League for their first competitive season.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> When <a href="/wiki/Edward_VII_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Edward VII of the United Kingdom">King Edward VII</a> granted Cardiff city status in 1905, the club put in a request to the <a href="/wiki/South_Wales_and_Monmouthshire_Football_Association" title="South Wales and Monmouthshire Football Association">South Wales and Monmouthshire Football Association</a> to change their name to Cardiff City.<sup id="cite_ref-obscure_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-obscure-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The request was turned down as they were deemed not to be playing at a high enough level. To enhance their standing, the team arranged to join the South Wales Amateur League in 1907. The following year they were granted permission to change the name of the club to Cardiff City.<sup id="cite_ref-Shepherd4_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shepherd4-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99–20_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99–20-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Although growing in stature, the club was forced to turn down the opportunity to join the newly formed Second Division of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Football_League" title="Southern Football League">Southern Football League</a> due to a lack of facilities at their Sophia Gardens ground. Over the next two years, Cardiff played friendlies against some of Britain's top professional sides, including <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_F.C." title="Middlesbrough F.C.">Middlesbrough</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bristol_City_F.C." title="Bristol City F.C.">Bristol City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crystal_Palace_F.C." title="Crystal Palace F.C.">Crystal Palace</a>. The matches were played at grounds in Cardiff and nearby towns so as to gauge the level of public interest in the team.<sup id="cite_ref-grandin12_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grandin12-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The club eventually secured land to build their own stadium, <a href="/wiki/Ninian_Park" title="Ninian Park">Ninian Park</a>, which was completed in 1910. The club turned professional the same year. They made their first signing the following year with the acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Jack_Evans_(Welsh_footballer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Jack Evans (Welsh footballer)">Jack Evans</a> from fellow Welsh side Cwmparc.<sup id="cite_ref-99–20_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99–20-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>With the new grounds in place, Cardiff joined the Southern Football League Second Division<sup id="cite_ref-FCHD_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FCHD-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> and appointed their first manager, <a href="/wiki/Davy_McDougall" title="Davy McDougall">Davy McDougall</a>, who became <a href="/wiki/Player-manager" class="mw-redirect" title="Player-manager">player-manager</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> They went on to finish in fourth place in their first year in the league. The board decided to replace McDougall with <a href="/wiki/Fred_Stewart_(football_manager)" title="Fred Stewart (football manager)">Fred Stewart</a>, who had previous managerial experience with <a href="/wiki/Stockport_County_F.C." title="Stockport County F.C.">Stockport County</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hayes208_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hayes208-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> He set about adopting a more professional approach, signing several players with Football League experience, including brothers <a href="/wiki/John_Burton_(footballer,_born_1885)" title="John Burton (footballer, born 1885)">John</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_Burton_(footballer)" title="George Burton (footballer)">George Burton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Billy_Hardy_(footballer)" title="Billy Hardy (footballer)">Billy Hardy</a>. Stewart led the team to promotion in his second season by winning the Second Division title. They remained in the First Division for the next decade, and finished in the top four on two occasions.<sup id="cite_ref-99–20_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99–20-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1920s_success_and_later_decline_.281920.E2.80.931945.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1920s_success_and_later_decline_(1920–1945)">1920s success and later decline (1920–1945)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cardiff_City_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1920s success and later decline (1920–1945)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1920, the club submitted a successful application to join the <a href="/wiki/English_Football_League" title="English Football League">Football League</a> and were placed into the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Second_Division" title="Football League Second Division">Second Division</a> for the <a href="/wiki/1920%E2%80%9321_in_English_football" title="1920–21 in English football">1920–21 season</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-99–20_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99–20-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Stewart brought in several players with Football League experience, breaking the club's transfer record on two occasions to sign <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Gill" title="Jimmy Gill">Jimmy Gill</a> and later <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Blair_(footballer,_born_1888)" title="Jimmy Blair (footballer, born 1888)">Jimmy Blair</a> from <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Wednesday_F.C." title="Sheffield Wednesday F.C.">The Wednesday</a>. They played their first match in the Football League on 28 August 1920, defeating Stockport County 5–2.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The side finished the season in second place to win promotion to the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_First_Division" title="Football League First Division">First Division</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FCHD_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FCHD-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> They finished behind <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_City_F.C." title="Birmingham City F.C.">Birmingham City</a> on <a href="/wiki/Goal_difference" title="Goal difference">goal average</a>, and reached the semi-final of the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20–47_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20–47-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> In their third season in the top-tier, the team finished runners-up to <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Town_A.F.C." title="Huddersfield Town A.F.C.">Huddersfield Town</a> because of a goal average difference of 0.024.<sup id="cite_ref-FCHD_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FCHD-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20–47_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20–47-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogeneratedqos_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogeneratedqos-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Cardiff drew their final match 0–0 as club record goalscorer <a href="/wiki/Len_Davies" title="Len Davies">Len Davies</a> missed a penalty.<sup id="cite_ref-20–47_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20–47-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:322px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CardiffCityFC_League_Performance.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/CardiffCityFC_League_Performance.svg/320px-CardiffCityFC_League_Performance.svg.png" decoding="async" width="320" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/CardiffCityFC_League_Performance.svg/480px-CardiffCityFC_League_Performance.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/CardiffCityFC_League_Performance.svg/640px-CardiffCityFC_League_Performance.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1047" data-file-height="500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CardiffCityFC_League_Performance.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Yearly table position since Cardiff City joined the Football League<sup id="cite_ref-FCHD_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FCHD-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/1924%E2%80%9325_in_English_football" title="1924–25 in English football">following season</a> was the first time Cardiff appeared at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1923)" title="Wembley Stadium (1923)">Wembley Stadium</a>, having reached their first FA Cup final.<sup id="cite_ref-FCHD_9-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FCHD-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The team lost 1–0 to <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_United_F.C." title="Sheffield United F.C.">Sheffield United</a> following a goal from <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> international <a href="/wiki/Fred_Tunstall" title="Fred Tunstall">Fred Tunstall</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20–47_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20–47-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/1926%E2%80%9327_in_English_football" title="1926–27 in English football">1926–27</a> season, when they finished in 14th position, was Cardiff's worst performance in the top tier of English Football since winning promotion six seasons before. However, they reached their second FA Cup final in the space of two years.<sup id="cite_ref-20–47_13-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20–47-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> On <a href="/wiki/St_George%27s_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="St George&#39;s Day">St George's Day</a>, 23 April 1927, at Wembley Stadium in London, Cardiff became the only non-English side to win the FA Cup by defeating <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> 1–0 in the <a href="/wiki/1927_FA_Cup_Final" title="1927 FA Cup Final">final</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hughie_Ferguson" title="Hughie Ferguson">Hughie Ferguson</a> scored the only goal of the game in the 74th minute. He received the ball from <a href="/wiki/Ernie_Curtis" title="Ernie Curtis">Ernie Curtis</a> and hurried a tame shot toward the goal;<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dan_Lewis_(footballer)" title="Dan Lewis (footballer)">Dan Lewis</a>, the Arsenal goalkeeper, allowed the shot to slip through his grasp and knocked the ball into the net with his elbow.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Captain <a href="/wiki/Fred_Keenor" title="Fred Keenor">Fred Keenor</a> received the FA Cup trophy at the end of the match from <a href="/wiki/George_V_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="George V of the United Kingdom">King George V</a> only seven years after Cardiff City had entered the Football League.<sup id="cite_ref-20–47_13-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20–47-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> When the team returned to Cardiff the next day, a crowd of around 150,000 people lined the streets to welcome them.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The side also won the <a href="/wiki/Welsh_Cup" title="Welsh Cup">Welsh Cup</a> in 1927 defeating <a href="/wiki/Rhyl_F.C." title="Rhyl F.C.">Rhyl</a> 2–0. They went on to win the <a href="/wiki/FA_Charity_Shield" class="mw-redirect" title="FA Charity Shield">FA Charity Shield</a> after beating amateur side <a href="/wiki/Corinthian_F.C." title="Corinthian F.C.">the Corinthians</a> 2–1 at <a href="/wiki/Stamford_Bridge_(stadium)" title="Stamford Bridge (stadium)">Stamford Bridge</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20–47_13-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20–47-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The club entered a period of decline after their cup success. They were relegated from the First Division in the <a href="/wiki/1928-29_in_English_football" class="mw-redirect" title="1928-29 in English football">1928–29</a> season, despite conceding fewer goals than any other side in the division.<sup id="cite_ref-28–29_table_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28–29_table-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> They suffered a second relegation two years later, dropping into the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Third_Division_South" title="Football League Third Division South">Third Division South</a> for the first time since they joined the Football League.<sup id="cite_ref-FCHD_9-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FCHD-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> During their first season in the division, Cardiff recorded their biggest-ever win when they beat <a href="/wiki/Thames_A.F.C." title="Thames A.F.C.">Thames</a> by a scoreline of 9–2.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> They finished the <a href="/wiki/1932%E2%80%9333_in_English_football" title="1932–33 in English football">1932–33 season</a> in 19th place, resulting in manager Fred Stewart tendering his resignation from his post after 22 years in charge.<sup id="cite_ref-20–47_13-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20–47-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Club founder Bartley Wilson stepped in to replace Stewart. Results continued to be disappointing and, in March 1934, <a href="/wiki/Ben_Watts-Jones" title="Ben Watts-Jones">Ben Watts-Jones</a> was given the opportunity to manage the club he had supported as a youngster. He was unable to turn the team's fortunes around; they finished the season at the bottom of the table, and had to apply for re-election to the league.<sup id="cite_ref-Hayes208_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hayes208-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Watts-Jones remained in charge for another three years until <a href="/wiki/Billy_Jennings_(Welsh_footballer)" title="Billy Jennings (Welsh footballer)">Bill Jennings</a> replaced him. Cardiff remained in the Third Division South until the Football League was suspended following the outbreak of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War&#160;II</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FCHD_9-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FCHD-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20–47_13-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20–47-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Post_war_and_European_competition_.281945.E2.80.932000.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Post_war_and_European_competition_(1945–2000)">Post war and European competition (1945–2000)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cardiff_City_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Post war and European competition (1945–2000)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In their first season since the resumption of the Football League, under new manager <a href="/wiki/Billy_McCandless" title="Billy McCandless">Billy McCandless</a>, Cardiff finished the <a href="/wiki/1946%E2%80%9347_in_English_football" title="1946–47 in English football">1946–47</a> season as champions of the Third Division South and returned to the Second Division.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> McCandless left the club soon after and was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Cyril_Spiers" title="Cyril Spiers">Cyril Spiers</a> who led the side to promotion in the <a href="/wiki/1951%E2%80%9352_in_English_football" title="1951–52 in English football">1951–52</a> season.<sup id="cite_ref-FCHD_9-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FCHD-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47–64_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47–64-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Cardiff returned to the top tier of English football for the first time in 23 years and stayed there for five seasons.<sup id="cite_ref-20–47_13-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20–47-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> They were relegated after in 1957, after struggling in the bottom half of the table for three seasons.<sup id="cite_ref-47–64_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47–64-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> They returned to the First Division for two seasons between 1960 and 1962 before they were again relegated.<sup id="cite_ref-FCHD_9-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FCHD-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Canton_End_at_Ninian_Park_geograph-2999342-by-Steve-Daniels.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A black and white image of a football match." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Canton_End_at_Ninian_Park_geograph-2999342-by-Steve-Daniels.jpg/220px-Canton_End_at_Ninian_Park_geograph-2999342-by-Steve-Daniels.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Canton_End_at_Ninian_Park_geograph-2999342-by-Steve-Daniels.jpg/330px-Canton_End_at_Ninian_Park_geograph-2999342-by-Steve-Daniels.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Canton_End_at_Ninian_Park_geograph-2999342-by-Steve-Daniels.jpg/440px-Canton_End_at_Ninian_Park_geograph-2999342-by-Steve-Daniels.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="969" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Canton_End_at_Ninian_Park_geograph-2999342-by-Steve-Daniels.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cardiff City playing <a href="/wiki/Oxford_United_F.C." title="Oxford United F.C.">Oxford United</a> at <a href="/wiki/Ninian_Park" title="Ninian Park">Ninian Park</a> in 1983</div></div></div>
<p>During the 1960s, Cardiff participated in <a href="/wiki/UEFA_competitions" title="UEFA competitions">European competition</a> for the first time as a result of winning the Welsh Cup, which granted qualification to the newly created <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup_Winners%27_Cup" title="UEFA Cup Winners&#39; Cup">European Cup Winners Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Their first ever match in European competition was in the tournament during the 1964–65 season against Danish side <a href="/wiki/Esbjerg_fB" title="Esbjerg fB">Esbjerg fB</a>. The team won 1–0 on aggregate over two legs, the only goal being scored by <a href="/wiki/Peter_King_(footballer_born_1943)" class="mw-redirect" title="Peter King (footballer born 1943)">Peter King</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> They went on to reach the quarter-finals before being knocked out by <a href="/wiki/Real_Zaragoza" title="Real Zaragoza">Real Zaragoza</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FCHD_9-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FCHD-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Despite their exploits in Europe, the team were still struggling in league competition under the stewardship of <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Scoular" title="Jimmy Scoular">Jimmy Scoular</a>, finishing in 20th position in the Second Division.<sup id="cite_ref-64–73_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64–73-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Two years later the team reached the semi-final of the Cup Winners Cup after victories over <a href="/wiki/Shamrock_Rovers_F.C." title="Shamrock Rovers F.C.">Shamrock Rovers</a>, <a href="/wiki/NAC_Breda" title="NAC Breda">NAC Breda</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Torpedo_Moscow" class="mw-redirect" title="Torpedo Moscow">Torpedo Moscow</a> set up a tie with German side <a href="/wiki/Hamburger_SV" title="Hamburger SV">Hamburg</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FCHD_9-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FCHD-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> whose squad contained several <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">German</a> internationals. This remains the furthest any Welsh side has advanced in European competition.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> After a 1–1 draw in the first leg, over 43,000 fans turned out at Ninian Park to watch Hamburg win 3–2.<sup id="cite_ref-64–73_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64–73-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/1970-71_in_English_football" class="mw-redirect" title="1970-71 in English football">1970–71</a> season, Cardiff reached the quarter-finals of the Cup Winners Cup where they faced Spanish side <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." class="mw-redirect" title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a>. The first leg of the tie was held at Ninian Park where 47,000 fans watched one of the most significant victories in Cardiff's history when <a href="/wiki/Brian_Clark_(footballer_born_1943)" class="mw-redirect" title="Brian Clark (footballer born 1943)">Brian Clark</a> headed in to give Cardiff a 1–0 win.<sup id="cite_ref-Shepherd4_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shepherd4-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> They were later eliminated after losing the second leg 2–0.<sup id="cite_ref-64–73_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64–73-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The team remained in the Second Division for 19 of the 20 seasons between 1962 and 1982. They were relegated to the Third Division for one season, that of 1975–76.<sup id="cite_ref-FCHD_9-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FCHD-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74–89_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74–89-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cardiff were continuously in the lower two divisions of the Football League between 1985 and 1993. The club appointed several managers in attempts to turn the team's performances around with limited success.<sup id="cite_ref-74–89_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74–89-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> They were relegated to the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Fourth_Division" title="Football League Fourth Division">Fourth Division</a> once in the <a href="/wiki/1985-86_in_English_football" class="mw-redirect" title="1985-86 in English football">1985–86</a> season and, despite returning to the Third Division on two occasions, they finished in their lowest-ever league position in <a href="/wiki/1995%E2%80%9396_in_English_football" title="1995–96 in English football">1996</a>&#160;– 22nd of 24 in Division Three.<sup id="cite_ref-89–99_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89–99-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> In 1995, Cardiff and other Welsh clubs competing in English leagues were banned from entering the Welsh Cup by the <a href="/wiki/Football_Association_of_Wales" title="Football Association of Wales">Football Association of Wales</a> after pressure from <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> who did not want teams playing in two national cup competitions.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Their final match in the competition was a 2–1 defeat to Wrexham in the <a href="/wiki/1995_Welsh_Cup_Final" title="1995 Welsh Cup Final">1995 final</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FCHD_9-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FCHD-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Foreign_investment_.282000.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_investment_(2000–present)">Foreign investment (2000–present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cardiff_City_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Foreign investment (2000–present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In August 2000, Lebanese businessman <a href="/wiki/Sam_Hammam" title="Sam Hammam">Sam Hammam</a> purchased control of the club and replaced Steve Borley as chairman.<sup id="cite_ref-Ignition_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ignition-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-chairmen_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chairmen-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Shortly after taking over, he controversially pledged to get the entire Welsh nation to support Cardiff by renaming the club "The Cardiff Celts" and changing the club colours to green, red and white.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> After lengthy talks with senior players and fans, he decided the best policy was not to change the name of the club. The club crest was redesigned; the new design incorporated the Cardiff City bluebird in front of the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Saint_David" title="Flag of Saint David">Flag of Saint David</a> and featured the club's nickname superimposed at the top of the crest.<sup id="cite_ref-Historical_Kits_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Kits-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Hammam funded the transfers of several new players to the club, and new manager <a href="/wiki/Lennie_Lawrence" title="Lennie Lawrence">Lennie Lawrence</a> guided Cardiff to promotion when they won the Second Division play-off in <a href="/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_in_English_football" title="2002–03 in English football">2003</a> against <a href="/wiki/Queens_Park_Rangers_F.C." title="Queens Park Rangers F.C.">Queens Park Rangers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Substitute <a href="/wiki/Andy_Campbell" title="Andy Campbell">Andy Campbell</a> came off the bench to score the only goal in extra time and ensure Cardiff's return to Division One after an 18-year absence.<sup id="cite_ref-Ignition_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ignition-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The club experienced increasing financial difficulties over the next few years and plans for a new stadium failed to gain approval from <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_Council" title="Cardiff Council">Cardiff Council</a> because of concerns over financial security in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-Ignition_35-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ignition-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Hammam then agreed to a takeover by a consortium led by new chairman <a href="/wiki/Peter_Ridsdale" title="Peter Ridsdale">Peter Ridsdale</a> and the lead developer of the new stadium, Paul Guy.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> During the 2007–08 season, Cardiff reached the semi-final of the FA Cup for the first time in 81 years after beating Middlesbrough 2–0 on 9<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>March 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-Ignition_35-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ignition-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> After coming through their semi-final against <a href="/wiki/Barnsley_F.C." title="Barnsley F.C.">Barnsley</a> with a 1–0 win at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a> on 6<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>April with a goal from <a href="/wiki/Joe_Ledley" title="Joe Ledley">Joe Ledley</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> they eventually lost 1–0 to <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_F.C." title="Portsmouth F.C.">Portsmouth</a> in the final.<sup id="cite_ref-Ignition_35-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ignition-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cardiff_City_celebrations_2018.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A football team celebrating with a trophy" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Cardiff_City_celebrations_2018.jpg/220px-Cardiff_City_celebrations_2018.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Cardiff_City_celebrations_2018.jpg/330px-Cardiff_City_celebrations_2018.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Cardiff_City_celebrations_2018.jpg/440px-Cardiff_City_celebrations_2018.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3888" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cardiff_City_celebrations_2018.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cardiff City manager <a href="/wiki/Neil_Warnock" title="Neil Warnock">Neil Warnock</a> and players lift the <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_EFL_Championship" title="2017–18 EFL Championship">2017–18 EFL Championship</a> runner-up trophy</div></div></div>
<p>In May 2010, <a href="/wiki/Chan_Tien_Ghee" title="Chan Tien Ghee">Datuk Chan Tien Ghee</a> took over as club chairman following a takeover bid by a Malaysian consortium; <a href="/wiki/Vincent_Tan" title="Vincent Tan">Vincent Tan</a> also invested and joined the board.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Tan later became the Cardiff's majority shareholder after buying out several other directors and acquired around 82% of the club's shares.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, the club appointed <a href="/wiki/Malky_Mackay" title="Malky Mackay">Malky Mackay</a> as manager.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> He took the side to the <a href="/wiki/EFL_Cup" title="EFL Cup">League Cup</a> final for the first time in the club's history during his first season.<sup id="cite_ref-FCHD_9-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FCHD-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The following season, Cardiff won the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Football_League_Championship" title="2012–13 Football League Championship">2012–13 Championship</a> title and with it gained promotion to the top tier of English football for the first time after 52 years.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> On 18 August 2013, Cardiff played their first ever away Premier League match against <a href="/wiki/West_Ham_United_F.C." title="West Ham United F.C.">West Ham United</a>, losing 2–0.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Cardiff won only three games in the first half of the season and, on 27 December 2013, Mackay was sacked by Vincent Tan and replaced by <a href="/wiki/Ole_Gunnar_Solskj%C3%A6r" title="Ole Gunnar Solskjær">Ole Gunnar Solskjær</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Despite the change in management, Cardiff were relegated to the Championship after a single season following a 3–0 away defeat to <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Solskjær himself was sacked on 18 September 2014 after a disappointing start to the following Championship season, and replaced by <a href="/wiki/Leyton_Orient_F.C." title="Leyton Orient F.C.">Leyton Orient</a> manager <a href="/wiki/Russell_Slade" title="Russell Slade">Russell Slade</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2016, <a href="/wiki/Neil_Warnock" title="Neil Warnock">Neil Warnock</a> was appointed first team manager of Cardiff.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Warnock took over the team with Cardiff second from the bottom of the table after two wins from eleven games, and guided the side to a 12th-placed finish after a good run of form.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> The start of the 2017–18 season saw Cardiff break a club record by winning their opening three league games of a season, the first time in the club's 107-year professional history.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> They proceeded to clinch promotion to the Premier League after finishing second in the table.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> However, they were relegated back to the Championship after a single season.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Support">Support</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cardiff_City_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Support">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Cardiff has a large catchment area from which to draw its supporter base. With only two professional teams (Swansea City and <a href="/wiki/Newport_County_A.F.C." title="Newport County A.F.C.">Newport County</a>) sharing the South Wales region, the nearest being around 40 miles (64 kilometres) away, the club enjoys considerable support from both the city of Cardiff and the surrounding <a href="/wiki/South_Wales_Valleys" title="South Wales Valleys">South Wales Valleys</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Identity_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Identity-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> As a Welsh club playing in the English football league system, national identity is believed to be a major factor in fan support, and some of the club's matches are considered to be Welsh cross-border rivalries with England.<sup id="cite_ref-Identity_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Identity-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> During the 1980s, as the club struggled in the lower divisions of English football, crowds dropped to an average of 3,000 per match. An increase in the club's fortunes saw a steady improvement in crowd numbers. The average attendance at home fixtures rose from 3,594 to 12,522 in a five-year spell between 1997 and 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Promotion to the second tier in 2003 brought further increases in numbers. The opening of the Cardiff City Stadium led to average attendances reaching 20,000 fans, culminating with a high of 27,429 in the Premier League during the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Cardiff_City_F.C._season" title="2013–14 Cardiff City F.C. season">2013–14 season</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dwindle_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dwindle-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Despite the increase, the club is often regarded as attracting fewer spectators than similarly placed teams. This has been attributed to several factors such as the club's controversial change to red shirts between 2012 and 2015—some supporters being perceived as <a href="/wiki/Fan_loyalty" title="Fan loyalty">fairweather fans</a>, and a lack of atmosphere.<sup id="cite_ref-dwindle_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dwindle-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Canton_Stand_do_the_Ayatollah.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Canton_Stand_do_the_Ayatollah.jpg/220px-Canton_Stand_do_the_Ayatollah.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Canton_Stand_do_the_Ayatollah.jpg/330px-Canton_Stand_do_the_Ayatollah.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Canton_Stand_do_the_Ayatollah.jpg/440px-Canton_Stand_do_the_Ayatollah.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2640" data-file-height="1632" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Canton_Stand_do_the_Ayatollah.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cardiff City fans performing "<a href="/wiki/The_Ayatollah_(football_celebration)" title="The Ayatollah (football celebration)">the Ayatollah</a>" in 2011</div></div></div>
<p>Welsh national identity also contributes to the supporter culture of the club. "<a href="/wiki/Men_of_Harlech" title="Men of Harlech">Men of Harlech</a>", a song largely made famous by the 1964 film <i><a href="/wiki/Zulu_(1964_film)" title="Zulu (1964 film)">Zulu</a></i> which depicted a battle involving a Welsh regiment,<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> and "I'll Be There", a take on a miner's song that was popular during the <a href="/wiki/1926_United_Kingdom_general_strike" title="1926 United Kingdom general strike">1926 United Kingdom general strike</a>, are both frequently sung before and during matches.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Ayatollah_(football_celebration)" title="The Ayatollah (football celebration)">The Ayatollah</a>, an act involving raising both arms up and down above the head in a patting motion, has become synonymous with the club and its supporters as a celebratory gesture since its adoption in the early 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-ayatollah_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ayatollah-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> The action has become popular with Cardiff fans outside football to show support for the club with boxer <a href="/wiki/Nathan_Cleverly" title="Nathan Cleverly">Nathan Cleverly</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Olympic swimmer <a href="/wiki/David_Davies_(swimmer)" title="David Davies (swimmer)">David Davies</a> and rugby player <a href="/wiki/Gareth_Thomas_(rugby)" title="Gareth Thomas (rugby)">Gareth Thomas</a> all having performed the action at some points of their careers.<sup id="cite_ref-ayatollah_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ayatollah-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalry">Rivalry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cardiff_City_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Rivalry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/South_Wales_derby" title="South Wales derby">South Wales derby</a> and <a href="/wiki/Severnside_derby" title="Severnside derby">Severnside derby</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dean,_Mike_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Dean%2C_Mike_%282%29.jpg/150px-Dean%2C_Mike_%282%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="194" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Dean%2C_Mike_%282%29.jpg/225px-Dean%2C_Mike_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Dean%2C_Mike_%282%29.jpg/300px-Dean%2C_Mike_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="358" data-file-height="463" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dean,_Mike_(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Referee <a href="/wiki/Mike_Dean_(referee)" title="Mike Dean (referee)">Mike Dean</a> receiving treatment after being struck by a projectile in a <a href="/wiki/South_Wales_derby" title="South Wales derby">South Wales derby</a> in 2009</div></div></div>
<p>Known as the <a href="/wiki/South_Wales_derby" title="South Wales derby">South Wales derby</a>, Cardiff City's most significant rivalry is with nearby neighbours <a href="/wiki/Swansea_City_A.F.C." title="Swansea City A.F.C.">Swansea City</a>, and over 100 games have been played in all competitions between the sides. Swansea's first ever competitive fixture following their founding in 1912 was against Cardiff in the Southern Football League.<sup id="cite_ref-Hayes5_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hayes5-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The rivalry had been relatively friendly until the 1970s and 1980s. Economic issues, such as the <a href="/wiki/UK_miners%27_strike_(1984%E2%80%9385)" title="UK miners&#39; strike (1984–85)">UK miners' strike</a>, rivalry between the two cities and an increase in <a href="/wiki/Football_hooliganism" title="Football hooliganism">football hooliganism</a> led to numerous violent clashes between fans at the fixtures. One fixture in 1993 was dubbed "The Battle of Ninian Park" for its particularly severe violence and resulted in away fans being banned from attending any fixtures between the sides for four years.<sup id="cite_ref-guardderby_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardderby-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-derby_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-derby-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Cardiff player <a href="/wiki/Jason_Perry_(footballer)" title="Jason Perry (footballer)">Jason Perry</a> described the period as "the dark, dark days of the derby".<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> When the ban was dropped, "bubble trips" were introduced for away fans who can only attend fixtures in police escorted-convoys to travel to and from the stadium.<sup id="cite_ref-guardderby_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardderby-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-derby_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-derby-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Further political divide between the two cities was caused by the <a href="/wiki/1997_Welsh_devolution_referendum" title="1997 Welsh devolution referendum">Welsh devolution referendum in 1997</a> when Cardiff was chosen as the site for the newly created <a href="/wiki/Senedd" title="Senedd">Senedd</a>, despite the majority of the city voting against devolution.<sup id="cite_ref-derby_70-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-derby-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Swansea, which largely voted in favour of devolution, received funding for a <a href="/wiki/Wales_National_Pool" title="Wales National Pool">national swimming pool</a> instead.<sup id="cite_ref-derby_70-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-derby-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alan_Curtis_(footballer)" title="Alan Curtis (footballer)">Alan Curtis</a>, who played for both sides, commented, "I think Cardiff has always been perceived [...] to receive whatever funding is going around. It seems to me that everything gets channelled in that direction".<sup id="cite_ref-guardderby_69-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardderby-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> 
Further afield, the club has a rivalry with Bristol City, known as the <a href="/wiki/Severnside_derby" title="Severnside derby">Severnside derby</a>, and to a lesser extent, <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Rovers_F.C." title="Bristol Rovers F.C.">Bristol Rovers</a>. There is also a lesser rivalry with Welsh neighbours Newport County due to the proximity of the two Welsh cities; they have rarely played against each other since the 1980s due to Cardiff being in higher leagues. In total they have only ever played 20 Football League games against each other. A survey by <a href="/wiki/Football_Fans_Census" title="Football Fans Census">Football Fans Census</a> in 2003 saw Swansea, Bristol City and Newport listed as Cardiff's main three rivalries, <a href="/wiki/Stoke_City_F.C." title="Stoke City F.C.">Stoke City</a> matching Newport in third.<sup id="cite_ref-Rivalry_Uncovered!_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rivalry_Uncovered!-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 1980s, a hooligan group known as the <a href="/wiki/Soul_Crew" title="Soul Crew">Soul Crew</a> emerged from within the club's fanbase.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The group became notorious for their violent clashes with rival supporters and have seen brawls between sets of supporters at football matches and other events.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Stadia">Stadia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cardiff_City_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Stadia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ninian_Park">Ninian Park</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cardiff_City_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Ninian Park">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ninian_Park" title="Ninian Park">Ninian Park</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ninian_Park_Cardiff.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Ninian_Park_Cardiff.jpg/200px-Ninian_Park_Cardiff.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Ninian_Park_Cardiff.jpg/300px-Ninian_Park_Cardiff.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Ninian_Park_Cardiff.jpg/400px-Ninian_Park_Cardiff.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="479" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ninian_Park_Cardiff.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The front of Ninian Park in 2005</div></div></div>
<p>Cardiff's first ground was at Sophia Gardens recreational park where they played from their founding in 1899 until 1910.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> With increasing support for the club, Bartley Wilson contacted Bute Estate, who owned large amounts of Cardiff at the time, in an attempt to find land suitable for building a stadium. They eventually agreed on an area of waste ground on Sloper Road. The land was a former rubbish tip and required extensive work to get a playable surface, but with the assistance of Cardiff Corporation and volunteers the work was completed.<sup id="cite_ref-grandin12_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grandin12-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The original intention was to name the ground Sloper Park,<sup id="cite_ref-Hayes7_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hayes7-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> but Ninian Park was chosen instead after <a href="/wiki/Lord_Ninian_Crichton-Stuart" title="Lord Ninian Crichton-Stuart">Lord Ninian Crichton-Stuart</a>, who was a driving force behind the ground's construction.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> The ground hosted its first match on 1<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>September 1910 with a friendly against <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa_F.C." title="Aston Villa F.C.">Aston Villa</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-Shepherd4_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shepherd4-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Lord Crichton-Stuart ceremoniously kicked off the game.<sup id="cite_ref-Hayes7_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hayes7-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The stadium was built with one stand. A second, which replaced an earth embankment and could hold 18,000 people, was opened in 1928. It hosted its first international match in March 1911 with a Welsh match against <a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_football_team" title="Scotland national football team">Scotland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hayes7_78-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hayes7-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Towards the end of its lifespan, the ground was replaced for international fixtures by <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_Arms_Park" title="Cardiff Arms Park">Cardiff Arms Park</a> as doubts mounted over the safety of the aging ground.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> The club's record attendance in the ground is 57,893 which was achieved during a league match against Arsenal on 22 April 1953.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> The scaling down of grounds throughout the 1970s and 1980s due to safety fears, which saw the ground capacity fall to 22,000, meant that the record stood until the grounds' closure. In its final years of use, the club was forced to seek special dispensation from authorities to keep the remaining standing areas of the ground open beyond the three-year period given to clubs at Championship level or above to remove them.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cardiff_City_Stadium">Cardiff City Stadium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cardiff_City_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Cardiff City Stadium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_Stadium" title="Cardiff City Stadium">Cardiff City Stadium</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cardiff_City_Stadium_Pitch.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Cardiff_City_Stadium_Pitch.jpg/220px-Cardiff_City_Stadium_Pitch.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Cardiff_City_Stadium_Pitch.jpg/330px-Cardiff_City_Stadium_Pitch.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Cardiff_City_Stadium_Pitch.jpg/440px-Cardiff_City_Stadium_Pitch.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2136" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cardiff_City_Stadium_Pitch.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cardiff City Stadium pitch in 2010</div></div></div>
<p>In June 2009, the club completed construction of a 26,828-seat stadium on the site of the now-demolished old <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_Athletics_Stadium" title="Cardiff Athletics Stadium">Cardiff Athletics Stadium</a> at a cost of £48&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-NewGround_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewGround-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> The ground was named the "Cardiff City Stadium". Three of the four stands would keep the names used at Ninian Park—the Grange End, the Canton Stand and the Grandstand—and the fourth stand would be called the Ninian Stand.<sup id="cite_ref-NewGround_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewGround-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> The ground's naming rights were expected to be sold, the club hoping to generate up to £9&#160;million income; they remain unsold.<sup id="cite_ref-NewGround_84-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewGround-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Although a pre-season friendly against <a href="/wiki/Chasetown_F.C." title="Chasetown F.C.">Chasetown</a> was played at the ground with limited capacity to test safety features,<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> the stadium was officially opened with a friendly against Scottish side <a href="/wiki/Celtic_F.C." title="Celtic F.C.">Celtic</a> on 22 July 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> The first competitive match played at the ground was on 8<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>August 2009, the opening day of the 2009–10 season, as Cardiff won 4–0 over <a href="/wiki/Scunthorpe_United_F.C." title="Scunthorpe United F.C.">Scunthorpe United</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> When it opened, the <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_Blues" title="Cardiff Blues">Cardiff Blues</a> rugby union club left their Cardiff Arms Park home to share the new stadium with Cardiff City.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> The move proved unpopular among fans of the rugby club, which returned to Cardiff Arms Park in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A few years after the stadium was built, plans to upgrade and expand the stadium were initiated. The expansion plans were completed in August 2014, and the seating capacity was raised to 33,316. In March 2015, it was announced that the Ninian Stand extension was to be shut for the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Cardiff_City_F.C._season" title="2015–16 Cardiff City F.C. season">2015–16</a> season due to poor ticket sales, dropping the capacity to 27,978.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> It was reopened the following year due to an increase in demand for tickets.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Colours.2C_kit_and_crest"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Colours,_kit_and_crest">Colours, kit and crest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cardiff_City_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Colours, kit and crest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colours">Colours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cardiff_City_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Colours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>When Riverside A.F.C. was formed in 1899, the club used a chocolate-brown and amber checkered shirt.<sup id="cite_ref-obscure_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-obscure-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Following the club's name change to Cardiff City in 1908, they adopted a blue shirt and white or blue shorts and socks, although for the first nine years black socks were used. Kit changes over the club's history have included all blue kits, the introduction of a yellow vertical stripe during the 1970s and alternating blue stripes.<sup id="cite_ref-Historical_Kits_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Kits-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2012, Cardiff controversially changed their home kit colours from the traditional blue, white and yellow to red and black,<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> the first time the club had not worn blue as its primary colour since 1908. The crest was also changed to one in which the <a href="/wiki/Welsh_Dragon" title="Welsh Dragon">Welsh Dragon</a> was more prominent than the traditional bluebird. These changes were made to "appeal in 'international markets'" as part of a "major investment plan" unveiled by chairman Vincent Tan.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> The rebranding provoked strong opposition from the fans, who organised protest marches and demonstrations to voice their displeasure at the changes.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Despite Tan previously stating that the club would only return to wearing blue if another owner was found, on 9<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>January 2015, after three seasons playing in the red kit, the club reverted their home kit back to blue with a red away kit in a bid to "unite" the club.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table>
<tbody><tr>
<td><div class="thumb tright" style=""><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px"><div class="thumbimage noresize" style="width:120px;"><div style="width: 100px; margin: 0 auto; padding: 0;">
<div style="position: relative; left: 0px; top: 0px; width: 100px; height: 135px; margin: 0 auto; padding: 0;">
<div style="position: absolute; left: 0px; top: 0px; width: 31px; height: 59px; background-color: #7B3F00;"></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Crest_history">Crest history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cardiff_City_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Crest history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From 1908 Cardiff played in unadorned shirts. This changed in 1959, when they played in shirts with a simple crest featuring an image of a <a href="/wiki/Bluebird" title="Bluebird">bluebird</a>. The following season their shirts were plain and unadorned and remained so until 1965, when they played in shirts with the word "Bluebirds" embroidered.<sup id="cite_ref-Historical_Kits_38-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Kits-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> A new crest, similar to the one used previously, and again featuring a bluebird, was introduced in 1969. Variations of this crest have been used over the years. In the 1980s, extra features including words and motifs were added. A major change was made in 2012, when owner Vincent Tan attempted to rebrand the club to expand its appeal outside Wales.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> This change gave large prominence to the Welsh Dragon, reducing the bluebird to a minor feature. In March 2015, Cardiff announced a new crest which would once again feature the Bluebird predominantly with a <a href="/wiki/Chinese_dragon" title="Chinese dragon">Chinese dragon</a> replacing the standard Welsh dragon.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Academy">Academy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cardiff_City_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Academy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For more details on this topic and current academy squads, see <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_F.C._Academy" title="Cardiff City F.C. Academy">Cardiff City F.C. Academy</a>.</div>
<p>Cardiff runs a youth academy catering to groups from ages seven to eighteen years.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> Recent players to come through the youth system include Wales internationals: <a href="/wiki/Joe_Ledley" title="Joe Ledley">Joe Ledley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Gunter" title="Chris Gunter">Chris Gunter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Ramsey" title="Aaron Ramsey">Aaron Ramsey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adam_Matthews" title="Adam Matthews">Adam Matthews</a>, <a href="/wiki/Darcy_Blake" title="Darcy Blake">Darcy Blake</a>, <a href="/wiki/Declan_John" title="Declan John">Declan John</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tom_Lockyer_(footballer)" title="Tom Lockyer (footballer)">Tom Lockyer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rabbi_Matondo" title="Rabbi Matondo">Rabbi Matondo</a> and,<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> prior to the youth system being granted academy status, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Earnshaw" title="Robert Earnshaw">Robert Earnshaw</a> and <a href="/wiki/James_Collins_(footballer)" class="mw-redirect" title="James Collins (footballer)">James Collins</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Records">Records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cardiff_City_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Cardiff_City_F.C._records_and_statistics" title="List of Cardiff City F.C. records and statistics">List of Cardiff City F.C. records and statistics</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gary_Medel_Cardiff_City.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Gary_Medel_Cardiff_City.jpg/220px-Gary_Medel_Cardiff_City.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="320" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Gary_Medel_Cardiff_City.jpg/330px-Gary_Medel_Cardiff_City.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Gary_Medel_Cardiff_City.jpg/440px-Gary_Medel_Cardiff_City.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1745" data-file-height="2537" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gary_Medel_Cardiff_City.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cardiff set club records when buying <a href="/wiki/Gary_Medel" title="Gary Medel">Gary Medel</a> in 2013 and selling him a year later</div></div></div>
<p>The record for the most appearances in all competitions is currently held by <a href="/wiki/Billy_Hardy_(footballer)" title="Billy Hardy (footballer)">Billy Hardy</a> who appeared in 590 matches for the club between 1911 and 1932, including in the Southern Football League.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Phil_Dwyer" title="Phil Dwyer">Phil Dwyer</a> has made the most appearances in the Football League era, having played in 575 matches. <a href="/wiki/Len_Davies" title="Len Davies">Len Davies</a> is the club's top goalscorer with 179 goals in all competitions. Seven other players, <a href="/wiki/Peter_King_(footballer,_born_1943)" title="Peter King (footballer, born 1943)">Peter King</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Earnshaw" title="Robert Earnshaw">Robert Earnshaw</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brian_Clark_(footballer,_born_1943)" title="Brian Clark (footballer, born 1943)">Brian Clark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carl_Dale" title="Carl Dale">Carl Dale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Derek_Tapscott" title="Derek Tapscott">Derek Tapscott</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Gill" title="Jimmy Gill">Jimmy Gill</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Toshack" title="John Toshack">John Toshack</a> have also scored 100 or more goals for the club.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Jack_Evans_(Welsh_footballer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Jack Evans (Welsh footballer)">Jack Evans</a> became the first Cardiff City player to win an international cap on 13 April 1912 when he represented <a href="/wiki/Wales_national_football_team" title="Wales national football team">Wales</a> in a 3–2 defeat of <a href="/wiki/Ireland_national_football_team_(1882%E2%80%931950)" title="Ireland national football team (1882–1950)">Ireland</a>. The player who has won the most caps as a Cardiff player is <a href="/wiki/Alf_Sherwood" title="Alf Sherwood">Alf Sherwood</a> who won 39 caps for Wales during his spell with the club.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> The highest transfer fee the club has paid for a player is £15&#160;million for <a href="/wiki/Emiliano_Sala" title="Emiliano Sala">Emiliano Sala</a> from <a href="/wiki/FC_Nantes" title="FC Nantes">Nantes</a> in January 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> Two days after signing, Sala died in a <a href="/wiki/2019_Piper_PA-46_Malibu_crash" class="mw-redirect" title="2019 Piper PA-46 Malibu crash">plane crash</a> in the English Channel.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gary_Medel" title="Gary Medel">Gary Medel</a> became the most expensive player sold by the club when he joined <a href="/wiki/Inter_Milan" title="Inter Milan">Inter Milan</a> for £10&#160;million in August 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cardiff's largest victory was a 16–0 victory over <a href="/wiki/Knighton_Town_F.C." title="Knighton Town F.C.">Knighton Town</a> in the fifth round of the Welsh Cup in 1962. Their biggest league victory was a 9–2 victory over Thames on 6<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>February 1932; their biggest FA Cup victory was an 8–0 victory over <a href="/wiki/Enfield_F.C." title="Enfield F.C.">Enfield</a> on 28 November 1931.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honours">Honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cardiff_City_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Cardiff City's honours include the following:<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="League">League</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cardiff_City_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: League">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b><a href="/wiki/Football_League_First_Division" title="Football League First Division">First Division</a> (As first tier)</b>
</p>
<ul><li>Runners-up: <a href="/wiki/1923%E2%80%9324_in_English_football" title="1923–24 in English football">1923–24</a></li></ul>
<p><b><a href="/wiki/Football_League_Second_Division" title="Football League Second Division">Second Division</a> / <a href="/wiki/EFL_Championship" title="EFL Championship">Championship</a> (As second tier)</b>
</p>
<ul><li><b>Champions:</b> <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Football_League" title="2012–13 Football League">2012–13</a></li>
<li>Runners-up: <a href="/wiki/1920%E2%80%9321_Football_League" title="1920–21 Football League">1920–21</a>, <a href="/wiki/1951%E2%80%9352_Football_League" title="1951–52 Football League">1951–52</a>, <a href="/wiki/1959%E2%80%9360_Football_League" title="1959–60 Football League">1959–60</a>, <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_English_Football_League" title="2017–18 English Football League">2017–18</a></li></ul>
<p><b><a href="/wiki/Football_League_Third_Division_South" title="Football League Third Division South">Third Division South</a> / <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Third_Division" title="Football League Third Division">Third Division</a> (As third tier)</b>
</p>
<ul><li><b>Champions:</b> <a href="/wiki/1946%E2%80%9347_Football_League" title="1946–47 Football League">1946–47</a> (South)</li>
<li>Runners-up: <a href="/wiki/1975%E2%80%9376_Football_League" title="1975–76 Football League">1975–76</a>, <a href="/wiki/1982%E2%80%9383_Football_League" title="1982–83 Football League">1982–83</a></li></ul>
<p><b><a href="/wiki/Football_League_Fourth_Division" title="Football League Fourth Division">Fourth Division</a> / <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Third_Division" title="Football League Third Division">Third Division</a> (As fourth tier)</b>

<ul><li><b>Champions:</b> <a href="/wiki/1992%E2%80%9393_Football_League" title="1992–93 Football League">1992–93</a></li>
<li>Runners-up: <a href="/wiki/1987%E2%80%9388_Football_League" title="1987–88 Football League">1987–88</a>, <a href="/wiki/2000%E2%80%9301_Football_League" title="2000–01 Football League">2000–01</a></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cup">Cup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cardiff_City_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Cup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
